"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. The man has 6 different types of fruit to choose from for breakfast.\n2. The man has 8 different types of vegetables to choose from for dinner.\n3. He can only eat one type of fruit for breakfast.\n4. He can only eat one type of vegetable for dinner.\n5. To find the total number of ways he can choose one type of fruit for breakfast and one type of vegetable for dinner, we multiply the number of choices for breakfast by the number of choices for dinner.\n\nCalculation:\n- Number of ways to choose a fruit for breakfast = 6\n- Number of ways to choose a vegetable for dinner = 8\n- Total number of ways = 6 * 8 = 48\n\nTherefore, the man can choose one type of fruit for breakfast and one type of vegetable for dinner in 48 different ways.\n\nThe answer is C) 48."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Probability of a voter voting**: The probability that a registered voter in Burghtown voted in the last election is 90%, or 0.9.\n\n2. **Probability of a voter not voting**: The probability that a registered voter did not vote is 1 - 0.9 = 0.1.\n\n3. **Number of voters chosen**: We are choosing 5 registered voters at random.\n\n4. **Objective**: We need to find the probability that exactly 4 out of these 5 voters voted in the last election.\n\n5. **Binomial Probability Formula**: The probability of exactly \\( k \\) successes (voters who voted) in \\( n \\) trials (voters chosen) is given by the binomial probability formula:\n   \\[\n   P(X = k) = \\binom{n}{k} \\cdot p^k \\cdot (1-p)^{n-k}\n   \\]\n   where:\n   - \\( \\binom{n}{k} \\) is the binomial coefficient, calculated as \\( \\frac{n!}{k!(n-k)!} \\)\n   - \\( p \\) is the probability of success on a single trial\n   - \\( n \\) is the number of trials\n   - \\( k \\) is the number of successes\n\n6. **Substitute the values**:\n   - \\( n = 5 \\)\n   - \\( k = 4 \\)\n   - \\( p = 0.9 \\)\n\n7. **Calculate the binomial coefficient**:\n   \\[\n   \\binom{5}{4} = \\frac{5!}{4! \\cdot 1!} = 5\n   \\]\n\n8. **Calculate the probability**:\n   \\[\n   P(X = 4) = 5 \\cdot (0.9)^4 \\cdot (0.1)^1\n   \\]\n\n9. **Calculate each part**:\n   - \\( (0.9)^4 = 0.6561 \\)\n   - \\( (0.1)^1 = 0.1 \\)\n\n10. **Combine the calculations**:\n    \\[\n    P(X = 4) = 5 \\cdot 0.6561 \\cdot 0.1 = 0.32805\n    \\]\n\n11. **Convert to percentage**: Multiply by 100 to convert the probability to a percentage:\n    \\[\n    0.32805 \\times 100 \\approx 32.8\\%\n    \\]\n\nThe approximate likelihood that exactly four out of five randomly chosen registered voters in Burghtown voted in the last election is 32.8%.\n\nThe answer is B) 32.8%."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Determine the distance from home to work:**\n   - The worker drives from home to work in 9 minutes at an average rate of 20 kilometers per hour.\n   - First, convert the driving time from minutes to hours: 9 minutes = 9/60 hours = 0.15 hours.\n   - Use the formula for distance: Distance = Speed × Time.\n   - Distance = 20 km/h × 0.15 hours = 3 kilometers.\n\n2. **Calculate the time it takes to cycle the same distance:**\n   - The worker needs to cycle from home to work at an average rate of 6 kilometers per hour.\n   - Use the formula for time: Time = Distance / Speed.\n   - Time = 3 kilometers / 6 km/h = 0.5 hours.\n\n3. **Convert the cycling time from hours to minutes:**\n   - 0.5 hours = 0.5 × 60 minutes = 30 minutes.\n\nTherefore, it will take the worker 30 minutes to cycle from home to work. \n\nThe answer is A) 30."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Determine the rate at which P eats candies:**\n   - P can finish the entire jar in 10 minutes.\n   - Therefore, P's rate of eating is 1 jar per 10 minutes, or \\( \\frac{1}{10} \\) of the jar per minute.\n\n2. **Determine the rate at which Q eats candies:**\n   - Q can finish half the jar in 5 minutes.\n   - Therefore, Q can finish the entire jar in 10 minutes (since 5 minutes for half the jar implies 10 minutes for the full jar).\n   - Q's rate of eating is also 1 jar per 10 minutes, or \\( \\frac{1}{10} \\) of the jar per minute.\n\n3. **Calculate the combined rate of P and Q eating together:**\n   - Since both P and Q are eating simultaneously, their combined rate is the sum of their individual rates.\n   - Combined rate = P's rate + Q's rate = \\( \\frac{1}{10} + \\frac{1}{10} = \\frac{2}{10} = \\frac{1}{5} \\) of the jar per minute.\n\n4. **Determine the time taken to finish the jar together:**\n   - If their combined rate is \\( \\frac{1}{5} \\) of the jar per minute, it means they can finish the entire jar in 5 minutes.\n\nTherefore, it would take them 5 minutes to empty the jar when eating simultaneously.\n\nThe answer is B) 5."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Selling Price of One Bag of Ice**: $1.25\n2. **Profit Margin per Bag**: 20%\n3. **Number of Bags Sold**: 500\n\nTo find the total profit, we need to calculate the profit made on each bag and then multiply it by the number of bags sold.\n\n4. **Calculate the Profit per Bag**:\n   - The profit margin is 20% of the selling price.\n   - Profit per bag = 20% of $1.25 = 0.20 * $1.25 = $0.25\n\n5. **Calculate the Total Profit**:\n   - Total profit = Profit per bag * Number of bags sold\n   - Total profit = $0.25 * 500 = $125\n\nTherefore, the total profit the grocery makes from selling 500 bags of ice is $125.\n\nThe answer is A) 125."
